<Name>Rachel Veley<//Name>< time>
1577763748050</time>
<Rate>1< /Rate>< review>
I had been a customer with Meineke here in San Luis Obispo for 5 years, without any issues or problems. I had always felt their prices to be reasonable and treatment of me as a customer fair. That all changed on December 19th. I made an appointment for my rear brakes to be replaced and an oil change. Dropped the car off at 9am and asked when it would be ready. I was told by Richard (the owner) that he expected the work to be completed between 12:30 -1:00 pm. I was at lunch and called in between that timeframe to ask how my car was coming along. I was told the work hadn't been done yet as the parts weren't available in SLO. Richard did not realize my 1996 Toyota Corolla had drum cylinders in the back. Did not realize. Guess he was not able to look up required parts to a car that had an appointment 4 days in advance. I let it go. Finally I picked my car up after my shift at work, around 5:00 pm. I got in and immediately noticed a sort of clunking sound coming from the right rear, as though a part was hitting against the wheel or something. I drove cautiously and called first thing Friday morning on the 20th. Richard told me to bring the car in and that they would look into it. I got a call from a technician, Victor, a couple hours later. He stated he wasn't the mechanic that worked on my car the previous day, but he looked at the car and there didn't appear to be a problem. I ask Victor if he had driven the car, to hear the sound... he actually told me no. I told him to call me back after he drove my car. It became very apparent to me at this point that no one at Meineke has probably driven my car, not even a test drive on Thursday after replacing brakes! Who doesn't test drive a car after replacing brakes, or after a customer returns the following day complaining of a sound!? So, after that call I called my family mechanic. Explained what was going on and asked his opinion. He said that sound will happen when drum cylinders are not properly adjusted, as what I have has to be manually adjusted. I laughed because when I was on the phone with Victor at Meincke, he told me that the sound was probably due to my front brakes being bad. That I didn't notice it until I fixed my rear brakes. He even offered me a quote for the repair! Absurd. Victor went on to tell me that rear cylinders are manually adjusted and that they can sometimes be off. I asked if he was stating that was why my car was making the noise in the right rear. Victor told me no, it was the front brakes, after all they were at 4mm. So, I called and asked to speak with Richard the owner. I told Richard to be sure my car was off the rack and parked, I was on my way to pick it up. Suddenly, just miraculously, my car was not making a sound when I drove it off the lot. The sound I heard, as well as two other people. I just wanted them to admit a potential error on their part, instead I was made to feel incompetent and unknowing. I was offered a quote for further work, when I was clear that I was unhappy with work completed just the day before. I took my car to my family mechanic the next day, Saturday December 21st. He measured my front brakes, which were just between 7mm and 8mm, so that was a lie told to me by Meincke. Then we checked by tire pressure, set to 30 PSI is the factory suggestion. I am visiting from Hawaii and visiting friends so you can understand my misery! I went back to my friends house and curled up in bed and hibernated in their guest room until New Years Eve when I decided I was either dying or I wished I was!

On going back in to the clinic with severe, and obvious, pulmonary distress I was advised to take a seat in the full waiting room. I politely told the desk clerk I was having difficulty breathing and I was informed it was first come first served. After listening to me try to breath (no joke I could NOT breath!) my friend, who had driven me because she didn't trust me to drive as I was, went to the counter and rather coldly told the clerk I could not breathe and I needed to be seen NOW!

I was seen almost immediately after that, lol. The doctor looked at my BP, oxygen levels, and chest sounds (around my coughing fits that left me limp and dizzy) and immediately told me I needed to be seen in the ER and I needed an ambulance and an oxygen bottle. My friend said that was good and she would meet me there. They called the ambulance and stayed with me until they arrived, giving me a breathing treatment while we waited. Turns out I had double pneumonia!

< text>
Laguna Beach Cliff Hike is a must if you're more interested in the unique often missed gems in Laguna Beach OR just want a cool run with good views :) The trail is perfect distance! Once you get higher up you will have two routes actually three if your interested exploring east. If you go the natural route to the top you have two layers of trails. Both trails are awesome once you get to the top you get a clear somewhat steep view of what appears to be The Montage golf course. Watchout for mountain lions and rattlesnakes, etc.<//text>

<name>Steven Engebretsen<//name>< Date>
1519333164500<//Date>
<Rating>5</Rating>< review>
This is a favorite hike for our family with great views of Laguna Beach! There are two approaches and one is more difficult than the other. The south trailhead is our favorite, but is more difficult. It begins in a residential neighborhood and ascends something like 600-650 feet in a matter of a 1/4-1/2 mile. With kids, this might be a little difficult. The other approach is from the East and is much more moderate because you park on top of a hill. When you come to the fork in the trail near the end, keep right to ascend to the tallest part of the peak. The views are excellent and there is a bench at the top. Beware of the sharp cliffs with the kids!</review>

I've shopped at Jim's for 30 years now and have never had a reason to go anywhere else. They always have what I'm looking for, and if not, they order it and get it there quickly. I am a professional musician and music instructor.  I have sent dozens and dozens of students to purchase from Jim's Music.  And I have personally purchased more than a dozen new instruments from Jim's myself.  They have been in the area, serving Orange County for decades.  They sell and rent thousands of instruments to the local school districts, and they outfit many area churches with their sound systems.  All of the staff is very knowledgable and professional, and they are not there to give input when they do not know the proper answer.  They also do not try to upset you, or give you advice just to get you to purchase something.  They are trusted people, and most of the staff are professional area musicians as well.  I send all of my students there, and have for fifteen years.  Great store, where you will normally get great service.</Text>

< user>
106474918725544300136< /user>
<name>Chase Lloyd</name><time>1342317756687< /time><Rating>3</Rating>< Text>
There's something cool about having a local music store. Maybe it's the underdog appeal or the campy appeal of walking into a business that has clearly taken over a few nearby store-fronts in its slow pace of success (sort of like the nearby Roma D'Italia), but you have to think about the customer base and whether you belong to it.

Jim's Music is in a good position to service the elderly residents of Tustin, who may be too put-off by the weird bazaar of instruments seen in Guitar Centers. I've been in shopping for parts and seen more than a fair share of Baby Boomers getting their strings replaced or their grandchildren fitted for a ukulele. On that note, I feel as if Jim's other big market-share is in the teenage band member population. A lion's share of their store is dedicated to band instruments, and you'd do well coming here rather than a Guitar Center if your kid needs a trombone.

So how about guitars? Chances are, you're better off buying a guitar online, even though Jim's has a very good history of matching and then beating online pricing. The only problem, therefore, is the stock on hand. There's a small selection to choose from, and chances are your crazy Ibanez guitar from Japan is not among the rows of ukuleles and Orange amps. So why else come here? Instrument repair! In my experience, the guys at Jim's do a fairly good job at whatever you throw at them... when they do manage to get around to it. I had a broken guitar in need of a new selector ordered from one of their partners. I called them back maybe three times to check on the part over the course of two weeks, each time being told that they'd let me know via phonecall when it would arrive. When the third week came, I took the beast to a GC and had it fixed a few days later; not only was I phoned back, I was able to speak with the technician via e-mail, which strikes me as a no brainer in this day and age.

As of 5 weeks after my initial ticket with Jim's, still no phone call. If you want your instrument repaired, you could bring it here... if you want it repaired quickly, look elsewhere. Your gig, recital, training regiment, etc. may depend on it.< /Text>
